## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the population growth rate dP/dt as a function of time t and population size P. Classical population dynamics models express growth rate as functions of current population (density-dependent growth) and sometimes time (for seasonality or changing environments).

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited growth, Malthusian model)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (growth rate decreases logarithmically with population)
- Theta-logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with shape parameter)
- Logistic with Allee effect: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P * c1 - 1) * (1 - c2 * P) (strong Allee effect, growth negative at low P)
- Von Bertalanffy-type: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolism vs catabolism scaling)
- Richards growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) * c3 (generalized asymmetric sigmoid growth)
- Linear decline model: dP_dt = c0 - c1 * P (immigration with density-dependent mortality)
- Quadratic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (higher-order density effects)
- Time-varying Malthusian: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t) (exponentially changing growth rate)
- Seasonal logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) (logistic with periodic forcing)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (fractional power density dependence)
- Harvesting model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P / (P + c3) (logistic with Holling type II harvesting)
- Beverton-Holt continuous: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) - c2 * P (saturating birth rate with linear death)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear proportionality to P (dP_dt ~ c*P) indicates density-independent exponential growth or decay
- Quadratic term in P (dP_dt ~ c*P - c*P^2) indicates pairwise competition or density-dependent logistic regulation
- Cubic terms in P (dP_dt ~ P*(P-a)*(K-P)) suggest Allee effects where small populations have negative growth
- Logarithmic dependence on P (dP_dt ~ P*log(K/P)) indicates Gompertz-type growth with multiplicative slowing
- Explicit time dependence suggests non-autonomous dynamics such as seasonal forcing or environmental change
- Ratio of polynomials in P (e.g., P/(1+P)) indicates saturating functional responses (Holling types)
- Fractional powers of P (P^c with 0<c<1) suggest surface-area-to-volume scaling in metabolic growth models
- Product of P with multiple linear factors in P indicates multiple equilibria (extinction, Allee threshold, carrying capacity)
- Sinusoidal time dependence multiplied by growth terms indicates periodic environmental forcing or seasonality
- Constant additive terms independent of P represent immigration or stocking effects
